O, sons, because I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by the fulfillment of it, the end is achieved in it, and by the expositions of it, and by the declarations of it, it is my view that you complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of the operation with my, so it is surgery.
Because the operation with my is prostrate in our region and in our time of all deprived, while many risk the science of it, and the vestiges of it are held hostage; and there remain of it only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered and become filled with errors and falsehoods, because their clauses are understood and the force of it and the art are elongated.
And it is seen to me that you vivify it with the order of this treatise in that according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and for that it may come with the forms of the tools of cautery and other instruments of the work, as it is for the addition of the declaration, and for the preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no one has been found a good artificer with his hand in this our time, is that the art of medicine is long, and that the one who acts it must before that be exercised in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia, because he knows the movements of the members and the forms of them, and the conjunction and separation of them; and he should have the knowledge of the bones, the nerves, and the cartilages, and the number of them, and the growth of them; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of the exit of them.
And for that reason, Hippocrates says that with a name is nothing, but in the work little, and most of all in the art of the hand.
But we have already said of that in the introduction of this book; because whoever is not learned in what we have said of anatomy, is not evacuated that he will not fall into error by which many men die, so as I have seen too many of those, who some are formed in this science and throw themselves from that science and their experiments.
Because I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed while the woman died among the hands of him.
And I saw another doctor who prescribed that the stomach of a man who had suffered in his state should be treated with a stone, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, so that that man on the third day died.
And I had already called to extract that, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the disposition of the patient, I knew about him that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was taking a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he came to a black peasant who was broken in his hip; and prepared the doctor with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, over the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and did not leave the wound to breathe.
And he soon let him go according to his desires, and he healed him, and he left him for a few days and commanded that we untie the ligament; and it was so that the hip and the leg were festering, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I prepared to untie the ligament, and obtained tranquility and then eased his pains.
But however, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, so that I could not restrain it, and it did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another doctor who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated after a few days, until the malice of it was magnified to its lord.
The cause is that the cauterized cancer is pure of melancholic humor, so that it does not come to it with iron of all, but that it be in a member which suffers that it be totally held hostage.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation with my hand be devised in two divisions: that is, in the operation that is associated with health, and in the work with which there is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already expressed this in all places of this book in which I present an operation that is error and fear; because it is necessary for you to guard this and leave that, so that the foolish ones do not have a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore, take your arms with diligence and with the protection of God, and your patients with facility and with firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, seeking health and praiseworthy success, and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult healing, and keep your arms from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: because more is left to your glory, and more so in the world and in the end to your sanctities.
Gualia already says in some of his admonitions: “Do not treat a bad illness, so that bad doctors are not named.”
And now I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and the first of the first part. The first chapter ordered of the head within feet, in the forms of instruments and in the tools of cauteries, and of that which is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of suction and perforation, and of leeches, and of poultices, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to those, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of sprains and of things similar to those; chapter ordered of the head within feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Know that you should say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its consequences, and in what completion it should be prohibited cautery.
Therefore I say that the sermon of the quality of the judgment of cautery and of its consequences is a long and prolix sermon, and subtle by science, and secret hidden; and already many wise men have spoken of it, and they have disagreed, and to me a little of their sermons suffices, fearing prolongation.
And therefore I say that cautery agrees to every universal completion, which is in matter or its matter, except for two completions, which are completions caused by its matter.
In the completion caused and dry by matter they disagreed; for some said that cautery is beneficial to that, and others said the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is inconvenient that illness caused and dry by that which is cauter and dry be healed.
And say that one who says the contrary of that, that by cautery is made benefit in all illness caused and dry which comes in the bodies of men, for when you compare the body of man and its humidities to the completion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say for the sermon of that, that experience has already to me some times discovered it.
But however, it does not behoove that it comes upon this that which is already exploited and exercised in the chapter of cautery by previous exercise, and has known the diversity of the completions of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their very selves, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the extent of time of those.
But in the other completions, there is no fear upon you, and more especially in the illnesses cold and humid, for already all the physicians have agreed upon those, and do not disagree in the judgment with cautery in those.
And know, children, that of the secret of healing by cautery with fire and of its goodness, it is because the fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and does not reach the other member attached to it except with little consequence.
But the action of comburent medicine reaches that in the members which are far from it, and greatly makes them come in the member illness of difficult healing and greatly causes them to be bad.
But fire, by its sublimity and of its substance goodness, does not do that except that it be superfluous. And it is already to us known by experiment and by the length of service of study in the art about the truth of the causes; and for that I am excused from the length of the sermon, and if it were not that it is not read in my book in this pause to you secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which it expels the illnesses, with a philosophical sermon demonstrative, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do cautery and pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because so that the consequence for the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which with the cautery is thrown, and more especially if the cautery is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulas, which do not suffer tardiness because it is feared of those that come malice, which is greater than little consequence entering by time.
And so do not catch in your minds, o, children, that this is not esteemed by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, so it is that to that illness which is healed by cautery is not reduced at all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not at all so as they care for that, because cautery is nothing but in place of medicine which alters the completion and dries the humidities which are the cause for which the pains come.
But however, cautery superflous upon medicine by the will of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness returns at any hour of time, according to the completion of the patient and the location of its illness, and the virtue of it, and that which is prepared in the body of it of the aggregation of the superfluities in it, and that which is reached to it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that the illness in which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and humidities, as well as cautery of a tooth for pain and things similar to that, it is possible that in it it does not return that pain, but rather that it is made in small.
And most commonly it is said that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, and it is a truer saying, for I do not understand those who use it, because I believe that there is no cure that will benefit with medicine or with any other cause better than cautery.
And the cause is the opposite; and the understanding that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the methods of cure in some illnesses, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause man administers cautery, and it benefits at that. And therefore, it is not according to the understanding which the vulgar and most foolish of the doctors understand that cautery is the last remedy of medicine.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen that and have found that it does not do so except in some bodies and others, and cautery with that is good and better than with iron as they said; but however when you do cautery with fire with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the roar of gold, and because it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust on it a fire it melts the gold with the fire, and in the fire some plates so that the artificer catches for the occupation of that.
And for this reason, cautery with iron must be done more lightly and more precisely in the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter in the cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that later the one who asks for it will know what they want from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and cold over the nerve affected by the accident of which there are two causes, so it is the cause of soda and multitude of rheumatic flux, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the ears and of the ears flow, and multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth and of the throat, and universally of all illness that comes from cold, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to what requires the virtue of the patient and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then do that sitting between your hands on a raised bench and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the razor of your palm near the nose between his heels. But however, as the tie your said of the middle place has arrived, sign that place with a tent, and then ignite the cautery olive of which this is the form:
And then place that on the place marked with a tent, in the manner that it descends, with which your hand be constricted little by little, and you revolve that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being discovered some quantity of the head, as well as the quantity of a grain of ears, then raise your hand, and if not turn your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone what I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that over the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a cloth soaked in butter and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with anguent tetrafarmacon until it is healed.
And they already said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more beneficial.
And they said some of them that it should be cauterized the bone inside the bone, and it should be held the cautery until some part of the surface of the bone is burned.
And then it is scraped that which is burned from the bone, and then it is cured.
And they said others that with the cautery it should reach the end, until it presses in the bone strongly, until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate that from that place the vapors of the head expire.
And it should be kept the wound open for a long time, and then it should be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cautery have not been seen at all, except in some men according to their fear; and leaving that, I, for my part, better is with health, when it is; because the head is devitalized by the solution of continuity of it as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the patient is of a cold nature.
And the species of cautery first is more safe and better, I think; and of that use and with that work with health.
Second Chapter.
Of the cautery of the head.
When throughout the head occurs chronic and long pain and this is prolonged in the patient, and use of herbs and potions and capipurgations and plasters and guats and cadels and gualinas and semblances, and mostly if it is already cauterized with a cautery which is recounted and does not profit him of any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and it is not frail and finds a very great heat, then that cauterizes with another cautery besides that one a little. And then cauterizes that one on the horn of his head with a cautery while the codena is parted. Incise the codena and uncover it from the bone the quantity which we have recounted and cauterizes that one with a cautery in the rear part of the head in the place which is called vas, — and is that place in which is placed a ventouse. And alleviate your hand in this, and do not uncover the bone, because the patient by this finds a great pain diverse from the pain of all the other cauteries of the head.
And you say this cautery in its place, because whoever cauterizes with the cautery with which the horns of the head and the occiput are cauterized is more subtle cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Three.
Of cauterization of  non-ancient migraine.
When it happens in the part of the head a sudden pain, or is extended pain within the eye, be evacuated with medicines the head modifying, and be administered the other cure, which I have said in the divisions of the diseases; and if nothing profits, then cauterization in it is in two ways: or cauterization with acute medicine comburent, or with iron.
But cauterizing with comburent medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and scour that one and abcise the extremities of it from both the heads. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet laid while it is in it made a place besides the codena, while it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopped by descent constriction, and leave that for the spaces of three hours; and then untie the and tear the alum, and leave the plague for two or for three days, and then place over it a cloth submerged in water while the place makes a scab.
And then cure that with an enguent while it is healed.
And if you want, do this with some comburent medicines the ones which I have written in the two treatises of comburent medicines.
But the cauterization with iron according to this manner: ignite with cautery of which this is the form:
And it is called claus clavilhs, because the head of it is as if in the form of a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle place of it is a small eminence.
And then place over the place of the pain, and retain your hand — so that not be burned the artery which is besides — and revolve the iron little by little with velocity.
And if the quantity of it that is burned by the proximity of the codena as much as the majority of it, and elevate your hand so that the artery which is besides is not burned, so that no come flux of blood.
And then imbibe cloth in salt water and place that over the place, and leave that for three days; and then place cloth mulled with water, and then cure with an enguent while it is healed.
And if you want, cauterize with the extremity of the cutler according to cautery, and guard yourself from incision of artery in this migraine properly non-ancient.

Chapter V.

Chapter VI.
Of the cauterization of tumors.
Tumors which are cured and by cauterization are nothing but of the kinds which come by phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the diseases.
Avoid cauterization of the species that should be due to dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of tumor with herbs and purgatives and gargles, and if you do not find comfort in your cure, then you must cauterize the ailment with three cauteries: the first you must at the root of the ear, the second a little below its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite of the diseased part, for softening does not come except in the part that is healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear, more sovereign a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which be according to the length of the finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the species of the code is burned.

Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, but that epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore, whoever modifies the brain of him at the beginning with years and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is great and tolerates the excess of the medicines.
And if it is a child who does not suffer the medicines, then administer safeguards and masticators to the brain, before that for many days, with the blessing of the foods.

Chapter XVI.
Of cautery of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted to the parts of the eyelids and pierce the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the parts of the eyelids so that they pierce the eye, cauterize in those in two manners, whether cauterize or is with burning medicine.

Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of a fistula that is in the lacrimal of the hand.
When you cure a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of diseases and do not confer your cure, then you must cauterize it according to this manner: command the patient to place his head on your lap, and hold his head some minister between your hands in such a manner that it is not disturbed nor agitated with his head.
And then place a cloth soaked in oil or in a poultice of ptilli on the hand of him.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
Which is concave, as is the form of a reed or a vulture's feather, at one extremity of which the cautery is made.
And if you wish, it should be penetrating into the other extremity. And if you wish, it should be shaped as a tent.
But however, that which is concave is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw from it blood and dry it out. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place on it the cautery which is well ignited, and take with that your hand a little from the cautery of the hand to the part of the nose, so that it does not burn your hand or the patient be agitated, and then place the cautery in the grain of the hand and corrupt it.
And therefore if at the beginning of your cauterization it penetrates into the bone, it is good; and if not, then iterate the cautery once or twice, if it is necessary; and leave it thus for three days, and then place on it a cloth with border and enclose it with an exsiccative enema until it is healed.
But if ten days had passed and it is not healed, then place on it an acute corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered and be scraped according to what you convene in your chapter.
And there is another manner of cauterizing a fistula which some first-dayers say:  enter at the place of the fistula and cut it open, and then place in that fissure a fine camel hair of which this is the form: And put in that the quantity of one ounce of molten lead; and take your hand with camel hair with good retention, and do not disturb the patient so that the molten lead does not reach the hand of him; and when you place on the hand of the patient a cloth soaked in oil or in water, because lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it by marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said of the cauterization and the cure, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer a traction of the nose and reduce the fistula to the nose according to what will come in its proper place.

Chapter XX.
Of cauterization of the teeth and of softening of the gums.
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are bad, and you cure those with medicines and do not confer, then place the head of the patient on your lap, and then ignite the cautery the form of which will come soon, so that you place the cautery on the tooth and introduce into it the ignited cautery quickly, and take your hand a little so that the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth being reached.
And then take your hand, and then iterate the cautery several times according to what you wish.
And then the patient rinses their mouth with salt water and keeps it there for an hour, then spits it out, because the bad tooth is stopped, the gum is softened and strengthened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
Chapter XXI.
Of cauterization of tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to cold, or there is a worm in it, or it does not respond to treatment with medicine, then cauterization is done in that case in two ways: cauterization with a cow's horn, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with horn is that you take a piece of cow horn and boil it in iron, then take a stick and wrap it around the tip of the tentacle, and then immerse that in the boiling horn, and place it on the painful tooth gently until it is scorched.
And then repeat that several times until the virtue of the fire reaches the root of the teeth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or a stick in the above-mentioned horn and place it on the painful tooth, and place a red-hot iron on top of it until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you attend to the tip of the iron or of the tool, and that it has some thickness in its center and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterizer, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it until the cauterizer is scorched; and do this several times because the pain will be reduced either on that day or the next day.
And so that by the impression of that cauterizer, the patient rinses their mouth with good broth and keeps it there for an hour and then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cauterizer.
And cauterize with whichever extremity you wish according to what is possible for you.
And this is the shape of the cannula:
Chapter XXII.

And then cure it with gargles and poultices and bandages until it is healed.

Chapter XLIII.
Of cauterization at the beginning of yellowing.
