Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of alconati.
This disease that is called alconati is nothing else but the one that is adjusted in the wound similar to a descending stream and is not that.
But the manner of working on it is that you make the patient lie on the prepared and straight saddle, and then take his head in your two hands and hold it so that you see the healing coming to the lower parts, and then let it dry and not descend, and let the light stay, and the patient sees the causes as he sees.
And if it does not descend below, you know that it is water.
But if the descent to the healing with water that we have said is not prepared, then make the patient lie between your hands and then take a fine spatula and  fen it on that over the panniculus, removing a little of the continuity of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the crown (within the empty place), until the healing is exuded.
Therefore, as it is exuded, then you distill into the wound water boiled in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey.
And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water from the wound.
We have already said the species of water in the division and which ones it is convenient to perforate with a sermo, declaring, then that one according to the health.
Then, you must make the patient lie between your hands on a cushion and tie his wound tightly.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of his wound if the wound where the water is is the left; or with your right hand, if the wound is the right.
And then with your right hand take an almond, if the wound is left; or with your left hand, if the wound is right.
And then place the tip of the almond near the crown for the thickness of the ray in the album of the wound from the side of the lacrimal gland, and then gently press the almond with virtue and turn your hand with it.
And then penetrate into the album of the wound and feel that the almond has already reached the void cause.
And it should be the measure of the path of the almond to the bottom the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the black, and it is the crown of the wound; for you will see with that pupil the vision of the eye through the clarity of the cornea.
And then place the almond into the place where the water is, and then you throw it down once, then another, and therefore if the water descends quickly, then immediately wet the patient's wound with water over which he sees his own vision, and the almond in his wound.
And then rest for a little; therefore if the water has descended, then you remove that other time until the almond is not thrown.
And therefore when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and turn it with your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little clear salt of gemma and with that wash the wound inside; and then place outside the wound a cloth or stopper or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white and lick the wound with water.
But in those who are of our time, place on that commi trissat with egg white.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the wound because of its hardness — for it is some of the men whose wound is hard very much — then you must take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the form:
And therefore, perforate with that that conjunction, and do not end your hand in the tract, and do not be unless you make a way for the almond to the subtle place.
And then introduce the almond according to what we have said.
And you must complete the work, having the patient lie down in a quiet, dark room, sleeping on their back, and prohibiting all movement.
And keep him in nature so that his nature be cleansed, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And bind him according to his disposition on the third day.
And after, in that dark room, remove the bandage and expose the foot to view, and have him see some things, and then return the bandage on the seventh day.
And do not let him do this at the time of healing or soon after the infusion. You must, however, let him do this when the water flows lightly and with great and vehement regard.
But if an abscess occurs, then you must unbind the bandage before the seventh day, and rectify it with water that brings the abscess to a head.
Then you cover his eyes and place a cloth on his face through which his breathing is regulated, leaving him in the dark room for some days.
And then withdraw him gradually from that room and converse with him about his ailments.
And know that in alchemy, the disciple is not excused from vision some times, and then you should be bold about the operation.
And we have now come to some of those who are in the Artach, and some said that they made a fire in the Ayrac almond, perforated with the one through which water is drawn.
But however, I have not seen any in our land who had perfected the water, nor have I read about it in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is new.
And these are the forms of the species of almond so that it may be above those who ignore them:
And they are made of brass or iron properly, and their extremities are with this triangular subtlety, the acute extremity as such is the form.
Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh wounds in the nose.
When in the nose there are born various growths, of which some are a cause that is assembled like a scorpion's tail, or a polyp; and this ailment is called a polyp because it resembles that tail represented. And of this, the flesh is cancerous, pale, of a dark color; and of this, the flesh is leonine not of a dark color.
Therefore, in that which is in these leonine flesh not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must have the ailment be seen between your hands and placed in the sun, and smear the nostrils of him, and prick your own finger on those flesh. And then extract that to the foreparts, and then incise that which you have comprehended of those with a sharp, subtle spatula from one part, as long as you know that all the flesh has been removed; if any cause of it remains, of which the abscission is possible, then you root that with one of the subtle instruments with ease, so that nothing of it remains. But if it bleeds or an abscess occurs, then you pause to him what you must; or if it is of malignant abscesses, then you cut and cauterize it so that it is abscised, and the cavities are all removed.
And then put in the nose after the incision, a mixture of wine and water or wine. But if the nose is open and from it proceeds humidity into the palate, then you know that it is already healed.
But if the humidity does not penetrate as it should, then you know that there is flesh in the pus, the leftover bones of the nostrils to which the abscission has not reached.
Therefore, then you must introduce a needle into him, to which there is some thickness, and sew in it wool thread, and place between each thread the quantity of a finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the needle into the nostril with the ray or with another cause which is possible to him.
And after that this has been done, that he may smell the odor of it until it reaches the canals of the nostrils, and be spit out on his throat, because many times the children in the schools do this action, and it is easier for him who wants to do it.
And then place the two extremities of the needle, one extremity that goes out over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a lock of flesh with the threads that are in the needle, and do this as long as you know that the flesh is already among the threads of the needle.
And then extract the needle, and place in the nose after the abstraction of the blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the engorged corrodes all that is left of the flesh.
And at the end of the cause, place in the nose a lead pipe for some days until it is healed.
But if you are in need of a cure that requires this, use of it.
And this is the form of the instrument to capipurge maker with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nostrils:
And make a pouch of silver or of copper, which is similar to a small open lamp, so like a small container, and the meat apparently.
And if you wish, make a closed tube like a cane, and the tube of the instrument to be a suction-maker and flat, uncovered; to which handle at the back of him, with which you have that when you heat it in oil or water that you want of the suckable causes.
Chapter XXV.
Of the nails in the extremities of the nose.
Many times the nail is seen in the extremities of the nose, and it is magnified and observed in certain days within which it is not possible to see its regard.
And for this, you must inscribe that at the beginning of its appearance, and you must inherit all that. And then put over the place the cautery or the medicine comburent the which was in the place of it.
But if its incision is late until it is magnified, then consider if it is calcified, hard, of brown color and of little feeling, then do not touch that with iron for it is a dangerous abscess; for many times to him who incides this abscess, evil comes to him who had it.
And if the abscess is of a lion's touch and is not of a dark color, and times that incision is possible in all of that, then evacuate the patient and incise that without fear, and cure the place with water that is needed and constrict within which it is healed.
Chapter XXVI.
Of the suture of the nose and of the lips and of the auricle when the continuity is dissolved by plague or by resemblances.
Know that when accidents happen dissolution of continuity in one of these cartilages, few confer in that operation unless in some men.
Therefore, when it happens to someone because of those, consider if it is fresh plague with its blood, and then you adjust the two lips of the plague with suture, and then cure that until it is healed.
And if the lips of the dissolution of continuity are already separated, and each one is made healthy, then you must excise each part of its apparent edge until blood comes out. And then adjust the two lips with suture and strengthen those, and over those pulverize blood of dragon and incense, and put over the powder a piece of diaphaniacon plaster, or of some other of the consolidating plasters, and leave that tied for two days or three, and then untie that and change that plaster and leave it until the threads are by themselves separated, and then cure with an enguent until it is healed.
But the manner of the suture is that you add the dissolution of continuity or with needles as we have recounted in the suture of the belly, or add the dissolution of continuity with thread as to you and it has been said.
Chapter XXVII.
Of the extraction of those causes that come in the two lips in the parts between them.
Many times it happens to many men in the parts between their lips some abscesses hard resembling fat of worms, and some of them are smaller and some are larger.
Therefore, you must convert the lips and open each of those hardnesses completely, and then the abscess you must fill the place with incense and until the blood is restrained, and then it must be washed with vinegar and the place must be cured with water that is astringent, until it is healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
Of incision of the flesh adjusted in the gums.
Greatly of times there is on the gum flesh adjusted the one which the ancients called albulus, therefore, you must suspend that with an onion or that which you have with the forceps and incise that you must see its root, and let the sania run or the blood.
And then put over the place incense or other astringent or excicative powders.
And if that flesh returns, then incise that secondarily, and cauterize that, for then the cautery will not return.
Chapter XXIX.
Of the reason of teeth with iron.
When on the surface of the teeth of the parts between them and of the front and between the gums are adjusted rough, jagged, and some times are of black and are made citrine or green until the gum sees through it corruption and are made the teeth jagged.
And therefore, you must make the patient lie between your hands and put the head of him in your lap, and grate the teeth in which appear those roughnesses and causes resembling sand until from them there remains no cause, and that do of the blackness and of the citrinity and of the others until they are modified.
Therefore, if this is what is at the beginning of the reason, it is good; and if not, then you repeat the reason on those on the other day and the second and the third until it comes to the last statement in what you want.
And know that the teeth have need of various forms and figures of tools according to how it is prepared for your operation. And for that the razors which the tooth is scraped from the root are different from the razors which are used between the teeth according to other forms, and these forms of razors you must prepare as you will see shortly:
Chapter .xxx.
Of Tooth Extraction.
Consider that you cure the tooth of its pain with all care and take your time in its entire extraction, because there is no reason to supply the void of it when it is extracted, because its substance sublimates while it is excused in its extraction.
But consider when the patient is forced to have that tooth extracted, that you must firmly certify which tooth is the painful one, because often the pain deceives the patient and makes them think it is in a healthy tooth, and you extract that one and the pain does not cease until the bad and painful tooth is extracted, because we have already seen this by the operation of the jaws.
Therefore, as you must certify which tooth is the painful one, and that you know well, then when you scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gums of all parts, and then you may with your fingers, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until that concaves.
And when you see that it is strong, take hold of it with great force for good speech or strong stupor, and place the head of the patient between your teeth that you well hold it so that it does not harm, and then pull the tooth according to rectitude in a manner that you do not break it, nor give the patient greater pain.
And therefore, if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and put that below it from all parts with facility and exert the removal of it as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then you must compress with cloth that break and tighten it with the extremity of a fine ray so that it is not broken in the hour of your constriction upon it with your grasp.
And you must work carefully with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gums and guard much your strength that you do not break it and remain a part of it, and return to the patient for the malice that may be greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their fisting and audacity over the extraction of theirs, because they do not administer what we have recommended; because often they make come upon men illnesses greater than those that are more difficult to be broken, and the roots of them remaugulated all, or some of those, or what you extract that with some bones of the jaw as many times as we have testified.
And after the extraction of it, the mouth should be washed with wine caut or wine with salt.
And if it is necessary to flow blood for this, as many times it is necessary, then sprinkle some quantity of zegi and sprinkle it over the wound, and if you do not confer this zegi, cauterize it.
The form of the forceps and subtle grasps with which the tooth is bad at the beginning be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they are not bent when with those you must work.
And be as times of thick handle so that when you tighten with those they are not bent, be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron, descentment made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those be teeth of which some are inturned in the others and tightened by strong constriction, and some times the extremities of those be the form of the beak of a bird which has the name of ciconia, so it is called, and are of strong constriction.
Chapter .xxx i.
Of Extraction of Teeth and Extraction of the Bones of the Jaw Broken.
When you must extract the tooth which is broken and there remains some cause, then you must place upon the place a poultice with border for a day or two until the place is softened; and then with some pliers or grasps the extremities of which are assembled to the beak of a bird called ciconia or guanta, the form of the forceps:
The extremities of those be made from the inside as a file or rasp.
And if you do not obey to your easement with these forceps or grasps, then you must dig upon the root and scrape all the flesh and introduce the instrument which has the name atali, so it is a small lever of which the form is this:
And be of short extremity thick a little, and not be embedded so that it is not broken.
Therefore, if by this the root is forced out, it is good; and if not, help yourself with these other instruments of which these are the forms: the form of the first instrument is of triangular extremity in which there is some thickness:
The shape of the second instrument is that it is triangular and of a very fine extremity.
And now you have helped with this instrument having two ramps of which this is the shape approaching the following: And with other instruments which I will describe in the shape of teeth; for help is made with this instrument which is assembled like a large onion, and this is the shape:
Of the triangular, twisted or short extremity, which is some thickness, and not buried so that it is not twisted.
And other know that the instruments of the teeth move so and similarly the other instruments.
But the skillful and subtle artificer in the art, finds for himself according to what to him signifies the operation and the diverse maladies; for there are maladies to which the ancients did not say nor posed proper instruments, for the forms of diverse species.
But if the bone of the jaw or of the other bones of the mouth is fractured, or if it may, then it should be cured upon that in its place with what is convenient to it of the instruments and the forceps which we have said in the extraction of the roots of the teeth, and help thee with the gesture of which this is the shape:
And let it be in it some thickness little by little, and be strung or held with the mouth so that it does not escape or flee until the bone of all is set; and then restore the place with medicines convenient to it.
But if in the bone is a small puncture, then rat that from that puncture and its blackness, and cure that until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the teeth eminent above the others.
When the teeth are eminent not according to their natural course, for those the shape is jagged, and more so when it befalls to women, and more so to the venerable old; therefore, as you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then root that; but that it not be annexed to another tooth, then you incise that with this instrument of which this is the shape; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and be made of Indian iron of a sharp extremity.
And let your incision be with which you incise that in several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and that it not be gnawed by other of the teeth.
And if the eminent tooth is exposed to filing, then file that with a file of Indian iron of which this is the shape:
And let it be all of Indian iron and the margin well-made; and be of very small points as a file with which needles are made, with which the tooth be filed little by little in several days with facility, so that it not be gnawed by other teeth and caga. And then line that at the end, and root that with some razors.
And if the tooth of which one part is fractured and it pricks the tongue, then as you file that until the expectation of that fracture be stayed and leveled, and be filled so that the tongue does not prick it nor the word be corrupted.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of restoration of teeth marred with wire of gold or of silver.
When accidents befall the teeth before concussion and removal by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot strengthen upon what he manages, and you have cured that with stiptic medicines, and it has not been of value your cure, then for so that it not be gnawed, it is engendered in those that are strengthened with wire of gold and not of silver, for silver becomes green and as soon as possible, but gold at no time is changed.
And let the wire be in such subtlety and thickness according to the quantity that it can enter between the teeth; and the form of the direction is that you take the wire and take the double of it between two healthy teeth, and as you increase with two tortuosities of the wire between two marred ones, or if one or many, until the thread reaches the healthy tooth of the other part. And then iterate the tressing into the part of which you commenced, and strengthen your hand with facility and saviness so that it not be marred.
And let your tightening with which you strengthen the wire be the roots of the teeth that it does not escape.
And then incise the extremities of the superfluous wire with the forceps or tweezers, and add those in each place with gesture, and convert those and conceal them between the healthy tooth and the marred tooth, so that it not do lesion to the tongue. And then loosen that as tightly as Roman.
But if it is loosened or broken, strengthen that or those with another wire in such a manner in all its time.
And this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the direction of two healthy teeth and of two marred ones, as well as sometimes these tied:
And when it is done that a tooth or two are returned to their places after the falling of each one, and they are recrescent as we have recounted, and that they are marred.
And this is done only by good artificers and wise.
And sometimes it is fitted some cause of the bones of cow, and it is made as such as the form of a tooth, and it is placed in the place in which the tooth fails, and it is strengthened as we have said, and remains and serves with that for a long time.
Chapter .xxxiv.
Of the incision of the ligament which comes in the tongue and prohibits speech.
This ligament which comes from the tongue some times or is natural with which man is born, or accidental and accidental by plague which is already consolidated.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient, his head existing in the tieu se; and elevate his tongue, and then cut that ligament nerve according to the latitude within which the tongue is loosened from its recess.
But if in that there is any hardness or knotting, and this is due to the consolidation of plague, then you cast an ounce and split that by the latitude within which you have incised the ligament and the knot is dissolved.
And guard yourself that no fissure is made in the skin of the flesh and that you split here the artery and blood comes.
And then wash the vestiges of the incision with water or with wine or with warm water; and then place the tongue loosely; so is the way which holds the patient's tongue in any night so that it is not consolidated again.
But if blood flows, place on the spot vitriol tri-sated; but if the blood comes, then cauterize the spot with a blunt cautery which convenes to this. And this cure with the other causes within which it is healed.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the extraction of a ranula from the tongue.
Sometimes a boil appears on the tongue resembling a small lump that prohibits the tongue from its natural operation; and often it is magnified within which the mouth is opened.
And the operation on it is that men open the mouth of the patient, seeing in front of the sun and consider the boil.
And if you see it of dark color or of black, hard, to which the patient feels no sensation, then do not touch that quarter for it is cancerous.
And if it is inclined to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then you put the ounce on it, and cut it with a subtle spatula, and cut it from all parts; and if blood comes to you in the hour of your operation, then you place desus zegi tri-sated, that is vitriol, within which the blood is restrained.
And then return to your work within which you had treated it with compliment of it, within which it is washed with wine and salt; and cure it with the other cure to water within which it is healed.
Chapter .xxxvi.
Of the extraction of a boil from the ears and of that which is nothing in the throat and of the other boils.
When in the throat there is a swelling, so are the glands which are assembled swollen, which sometimes appear outside and are called boils, which when you cure them with water that we have said in the division and it is not healed, then consider if the boil is hard, of dark color, of little sensation, then do not touch that with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is thick, then do not touch that with iron for the flow of blood; let it lie there within which it is ripened, and then either you will extract it, or it will be broken by itself.
And if it is of white color, radon, and the root of it is subtle, then that is the one that must be incised.
And the operation on it is that you consider, before your operation, if the boil has already rested of it covered with a complete repaus or if it is diminished with any diminution; and then do make the patient stand before the sun, and his head be in the tieu se, and open his mouth, and the servant takes between his hands presses the tongue of him from with a noble instrument of which this is the form:
And it is made of silver or of brass, and it is subtle with a point.
Then, as you press with that the tongue and it is shown to you the boil, and catch upon that your gaze, then take an ounce and place it in the middle, and pull that to the outside parts as much as you can. Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then cut that with the instrument of which this is the form:
Other water that you pull some cause of the tunics, and then cut that with the instrument of which this is the form: And it is assembled to forceps, however the extremities of it are curved, so that the orifice of each one is in the straight of the other, very sharp, the one which is of iron indi embedded.
But if this instrument is not to you present, then cut that with a spatula of which this is the form of it: And it is sharp on one part, not sharp on the other part.
And since you have incised one well, cut the other according to this same manner of incision, and then the incision the patient should wash with warm water
But if there is a flow of blood, wash with water of decoction of the bark of millefolium or of myrtle leaf and similar to those of the stiptic causes within which the flow of blood is restrained, and then cure it within which it is healed.
And sometimes there are born in the throat other boils other than those boils, and cut those according to what I have said in the incision of two wells equally.
And I had already treated a woman of an abscess that was located in the throat of her, the abscess tended to a brown color, of little feeling, the one that had already closed the throat of her, and the woman breathed with tight meat, and had already prohibited her from eating and drinking water, and she had already arrived at death if may agues stood for a day or two.
And the abscess had already grown so much that there were two fingers inside that it came out through two tracts.
Therefore, I thought to treat her fistularly and I stayed in one of them, and I pulled out that one, and it was thrown out of it a large portion, and then I incised that one from where I understood the other tract, and then I opened the mouth of it, and I compressed her tongue, and then I stayed the one in that abscess.
And then I abscessed a large portion of it, and it did not run from it but a little of blood. Therefore, the throat of that woman was absolutely opened, and she began to drink water, and then she ate food, so I did not stop inciding that abscess many times for a long time, and a new abscess succeeded in its place, the one that incised until it was prolonged.
Therefore, I brought a needle and cauterized the throat of her, so as to add no more; and then I walked around and I did not know what God did of that, after me.
Chapter .xxxvii.
Of incision of a boil when it is abscesses.
When catarr arises in the boil, and it is abscesses and it is long, then it is called perpendicular; and if it is in the part below thick and round, and then it is called bubo.
But when it is cured with what we have said in the division, and it does not confer your cure, and you see many times that the abscess cauterizes already it is gone from it and it is subtle, then cover that you incised the one that is aggregated round; and if it is at that longitude, and it is sanguine, of brown color or of black, and it is not felt in it, then cover that you attempt the incision of it, because in that there is fear about the patient.
And when you see that according to the manner that I have said of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient to be seen and press his tongue with an instrument of which you process its form and then stay the one in the new, and pull that one down and incise that one with one of the two instruments the ones that are said in the incision of two wells.
And cover that you do not incise that one but what is adjusted over the natural term its addition, because if you incise that one more, you will lead the one's speaking.
And after the incision, use of that which have been recommended in the incision of two wells, and cure that one until it is healed.
But if the patient were frightened by the incision of it, cover that you use of an engine in the cauterization of it its fear, and the manner of the cautery in it is not but with sharp water, and it is that you stay the head of the patient in your own, and then press the tongue of it with the instrument the one that we have said, and then take of the water the one that we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and confer with that cause alive, and stay that not thick nor subtle, and of that fill the concavity of the instrument of which this is the form:
Be the extramitat of it concavity in which is stayed the medicine as well as the concavity of a spoon of ray, and stay the instrument with the medicine over the boil, and the patient jagua over his latz so that it runs saliva or musellage of the mouth of that one by the intrinsic medicine, so that it does not descend from that one of any cause over the throat of it and that it leads that one.
And after your hand with the medicine, and express that one over the uvula for the space of a middle hour until you see that one being darkened and sedated by the bite of the medicine.
And if you want, take a cloth and envelopes that one over the extremity of the ray, and submerge the cloth in the medicine, and intermet the ray with the cloth in a canula of above until the cloth adheres in that canula, and do that many times until you achieve what you want of the cauterization of the uvula, and after that, lay that one because it dried and falls down after three days or four.
And if you indigeysses that you iterate the medicine, iterate that one, and after the cauterization abstergeys in the circuit of the uvula with cloth imbued in border, and modify with that which is in the circuit of it of the medicine, and be washed with cold water, and be cured for the moment with embrocation, and dedicate with gargarismes until it is healed.
And this kind of cure is more safe than incision and more long of fear.
Sometimes the uvula is cured with that which is more subtle than cauterization and incision, because it is cured with subfumigation in this manner: receive calament, ysop, origua, ruda, sicados arabic, camomilla, broyda and similar to those of the herbs, and adjust all those causes, or some of them, in an olla, and be submerged with hot wine, and boil; and the olla be well fought with lut decently, and be in the middle place of the olla a tract, over which is stayed an instrument concavity of ram according to this manner; be made of silver or of ram.
And the limb is inserted into the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the uvula above the pharynx, until the uvula is somewhat obscured.
And then repeat this process until it is dry, and be careful not to do this treatment at the beginning of the development of abscesses, because it would tighten too much on the abscess, and in the case that you do this, you should declare the abscess of the patient.
But if you do not have this instrument at present, then take a cane and on the end of it make a hollow of wax, so that the patient's mouth is covered, because the wax prevents the vapor from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Of the extraction of thorns and of what adheres in the throat and of other causes.
Many things adhere to the throat or a thorn of fish or some other cause.
Therefore, it is necessary that you extract what appears of those things, over which you place your gaze, because you press the tongue with an instrument in front of the sun, so that it is declared to you what is in the throat.
And what does not appear and is hidden to you in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach, because often the cause annexed to the throat is forced-out by vomiting; or that the patient swallows a piece of bread or a root of lettuce or a piece of dry bread; or  chew a piece of dried sea sponge, and tie it firmly with a thread, and then the patient swallows it, because when it reaches the place where the thorns are and are extracted, then they are forced-out. And more, take an eel and tie it with a thread, and it is placed and gently extracted; or take a pear and gently the stem and gently the bottom.
But if they are not forced-out with those causes which we have said, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:
And it is thicker than a ray, and at the end of it is a concavity which you insert into the patient's throat with ease.
And have the patient's head elevated upwards, and be careful that the touch of his bone of the throat, so that it does not break his body and with that which pushes the bone or the thorn, or that the physician with his hand.
But however, that the patient is more easily inserted, by his knowledge of the place of the annexed cause and pushes down, and pulls his hand with the instrument upwards, all this according to the quantity which is prepared for him before it is forced-out.
Chapter XXXIX.
Of the extraction of bloodsucker annexed to the throat.
When a leech is medicated with what we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you have examined the tongue of him with the instrument which we have recommended to you.
Therefore, if you see the leech, extract it with a small pin or with a subtle gesture gently.
And if it is not possible to extract with that, then take a concave tube and insert it into the patient's throat, and then place in the concavity of the tube a burning iron, and do this as many times (until the leech is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain the patient all day from water.
And then chew a full mouthful of cold water, and work the patient's mouth in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that and bad luck the water one hour after another with your hand, because the leech as soon as it feels the water catches.
But if it is not forced-out with what we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with cinnamon or with asafoetida with the instrument which we have recommended in the fumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so long as it falls.
And there is another way of operation in fumigation of that, which is that you take a bowl in which there are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a blanket in the middle of which there is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the end of the instrument; and then let go from below the fumigation; and have the patient put their mouth at the end of the tube, and clamp their mouth so that the fumigation is not forced-out until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech, because the leech will immediately fall.
And if it does not catch, then you repeat the fumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty and hot foods, and do not drink water, and thus it is necessary that with this regimen it be forced-out.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the leech of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: Which is placed in the throat, and the end of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is gripped, in which it is sharpened with a file, so that, when you grasp any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter XL.
In which is the sum of the discourse concerning abscesses and their incision.
Abscesses are certain kinds, of certain manners, according to the remembrance of them, of each in this book.
And they are diverse in their perforation and incision by two manners, of which one is by the species of abscesses themselves; and by that which we understand of the humidities.
And the second manner is according to the places in which they happen in the body, for the abscess that happens in the head is another from the abscess that happens in the buttock; and the abscess in the fleshy place is another from the abscess that happens in the joint; and to each of them is its own way of operation.
And more than abscesses are some which ought not to be perforated until the maturity of the healing in those or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses which ought to be lanced when they are ripe, and not until the completion of them, as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess is near a joint, its being is prolonged until it can exert that which is in the circuit of it, and then it is likely that the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, so that it becomes a cause of contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near a principal member, and if you delay the lancing of it until it is ripe, it will cause harm to the principal member; or it is near the buttock, therefore lance it before it is ripe; and you ought not to lance it crude, from incomplete digestion, but that which is near the buttock, so that you cannot make the prepuce of it and extend it to the parts behind the buttock, and make a fistula, or that it may be made in the term of it that it may not be healed. But more, you ought to know the hour of the lancing of the abscess, and thus it is when it is ripe.
And know that it is ripe when there is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and according to the diminution of the heat and of the pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you ought to know the lancing to be done in the place farthest from the abscess and of pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And lancing always should be done along the length of the flesh or of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the arms or of the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, lastly, in all places equal in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use of lancing according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, then it is best to let the lancing of it until the digestion of it is confirmed according to its completion, as we have said; for if you lance it before that, it prolongates the body of the pus of it and of much filth, and then very likely the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are lanced according to the width of the flesh or of the body as necessity demands, or according to that which the member indicates.
And you ought to administer little lancing, and in large abscesses a large lancing and many sections according to the variety of the greatness of the abscesses.
And others are of abscesses in which the wound ought to be concaved and be incised, when it is done so that it may be like bread and it is made in the term that it already sticks, as that which happens in troops of boils and buboes.
And of those are those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those is that in which it is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf, as the abscesses of the angles.
And of those are those in which a round section and a lunar section, and similar to those, are administered.
But that one to whom there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you ought to lance that with a superficial lancing, or plane only.
And you ought when the abscess is large and has already collected much pus, that you lance it and do not take that you extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted from it one part, and then plug the abscess until the next day, and then extract a larger part, and then do this many times according to gradation until it is all gone.
And most of all if the patient is of feeble virtue, or woman pregnant, or child small, or old in decrepitude, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the egress of the pus, and very likely the patient will die, and you operate on them.
Therefore guard this chapter with great care, and in the lancing of these abscesses, you ought to abstain from the plagues and consider therefore if the plague of the abscess is little, or is a plain section, then you administer the poultices of it or of a counter-poultice; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the lancing are many, then you ought to place a cloth in each one until they meet together.
And if in the abscess is cut off a part of the wound or has concaved that in the circuit, then you ought to cover it with a poultice of old cloth or a thread made of linen of it, as when you have treated loaves or roots, its humidity; and strengthen that in the third day; and then process that and cure it with that which you ought of the unguents until it is healed.
But if blood flow occurs during the time of the operation, then you administer cold water and sweet wine to the patient, mixing a cloth with them, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
But if the bleeding persists, then you must administer treatment and care, and follow the powders that I have recommended in many places in this book and its division.
But if it is in winter, and the place of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must put powders in wine and hot oil, and place them on the area.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you must place powders mixed with water and oil or with wine and oil, and all that be heated until the third day, as we have said, and then you must open the abscess and cleanse it and administer to it what is necessary for its healing.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of every abscess in what manner is the way of its cure by chapters individually.
Chapter .xli.
Of the incision of abscesses that come in the neck of the head.
In the neck of the head, small abscesses appear, and they are of a kind of nodes which contain tunics that are to their making; and the kinds of them are many.
And of them are pimples, and of those are those that contain moisture similar to lime. And of those are those that contain moisture similar to powder, and resembling them; and of those are those that are stony, hard.
And in the section of all of them, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must, the exterior of those does not cause artery opposition.
And the operation in the section of those is that you probe those with an instrument the shape of which comes near thus, the one which is called entromes, as long as you know that it contains.
Because if that which contains is moisture, then you cut that with a section according to the length by a superficial section according to this form:
And it begins in the section of the line of .B. into the line of .G. Therefore, as the moisture is evacuated, then you excoriate that skin that contains that moisture, and do not leave of that any cause of all, for troops many times return, if there remain of that any cause.
And then you submerge the wound in Egyptian wash, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill it with that the wound and leave it for another day, for with that you corrode all that is raw of that pellicle.
And then repeat over that wound with Egyptian wash second and third times if you judge it necessary, until you are confident that there is no raw cause of that pellicle; then cure the wound with wash until it is healed.
And if the abscess contains fatty nodes, then you incise it according to this form: with a section having the form of a cross, and get onces between the two lips of the section and scour that from all parts, and exert your strength in the extraction of the tunic which contains that.
But if your artery makes opposition, then do what I have recounted to you first.
And similarly do in the stony abscess of section and cure according to what we have said to you; and section over a stony abscess is lighter, because it is of little blood and of little moisture.
And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in some men with which there is no moisture at all; the cause of which is because I incised upon an abscess in the head of an old woman and retrieved the abscess as a hard, rough, white thing, which could not be squeezed, and if anyone was struck with that, it would bring them plague.
But in the other abscesses accidents in the head other than this one is not this chapter, as well as the abscesses that come to the heads of children and which you must root from the ears, but the section of all of these is a superficial section.
And pause the perforation of those from the lower part of them so that the body of the body be relieved of the sickness in the lower parts.
And then cure those with what is necessary for that cure.
Chapter .xlii.
Of the incision of scrophulas which occur in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groin; and sometimes they occur in the other parts of the body.
And those that occur in the neck, and are many that are generated among them, and all scrofulous of those is within its own tunic, and as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have recounted.
And the kinds of these scrofulas are many, for of those some are stony, and of those some contain humidities, and of those some are malignant ones which do not obey cure.
Therefore, in that one which you see of good disposition in the Touch, of which the color of that which is manifest is proper to the color of the neck, and is smooth in all parts, and is not annexed to the nerve of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the artery, and is not hard, then you must incise that with a superficial section from the lower part to the upper part of the body of the line of .G. into the line of .B., and scour that from all parts, and extend the lips of the neck with an onci, or with many onces if you have need of those, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract that little by little.
And it is more caution that the vein or nerve is not cut.
And let the spatula not be too sharp, so that you do not injure the patient with a cut, or that you cut what is not necessary to cut; for if you were to cut a vein or artery and you prohibit yourself from your operation, then apply a tri-smelted vitriol poultice or other powders which stop the flow of blood, and tighten the wound, and leave that within which the sharpness of the abscess rests and the wound is softened and begins to be pus-filled. When the blood is cut.
Therefore, return to your operation until you have completed it.
And then inquire with your little finger if there is any cause of other small abscesses, therefore cut those and cleanse them.
And if it is in the root of the large abscess, then cover it so that you do not cut that abscess from its root. Cover it so that you hold it with a strong double-folded cloth and let it remain within until it falls by itself.
And then fill the wound with old cloth which you have already submerged in Egyptian wash, and then cure it.
And if you cut that abscess completely, then cover it so that you adjust the two lips of the wound and sew them together as soon as pus comes out so that there is no superfluity.
But if you see that there is superfluity due to the size of the abscess, cover it so that you understand to cut the root of it, and extract it and administer suture and what has been said.
And those of the abscesses that contain humidity, perforate it with a superficial puncture where you see the place of maturation of it, and place a puncture of it so that it drains the pus from the bottom of the body, as we have said.
And then administer puncture, lukewarm washes and similar things to those, so that it corrodes what is rotten from the corruption. And then when you see the wound already cleansed, then cure it with a wash of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter .xliii.
Of the section of the pile of the abscess accidental within the gullet.
The ancients said this section in the epiglottis, and no one in our land has done it.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a squint, cover that the extraction of the epiglottis be avoided, as for that it is not done well for that all the veins and major arteries of the body are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or gullet or the two ears, when the illness is not in the canal, cover that you use the section of the epiglottis to avoid the damage which is done by perforation.
Therefore, when we want this, cover that they cut the epiglottis below three circles of the circles of the epiglottis, or four with a small section for the width in that which is between two circles by quantity, that the section be in cartilage, not in the flesh, and this place is convenient for section, because it is deprived of flesh and the blood vessels of it are there.
And if the physician is fearful, cover that he then extend the throat of the gullet with tongs, and then open the throat until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if he sees any cause of them.
And then cut the cartilage as we have recounted; and it is significant over the section of the canal by the flame which is of that it is emitted with what is of it discolored and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, when the hour is remauguda in which perforation is feared, add two lips of the throat of the wound, and sew that alone with the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recounted, exposure is nothing but that you see that some of these abscesses have already opened the gullet of the patient, and the patient has come to death, and the skin of it is dried up, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by any respiration, and be saved from death.
And for that reason command to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then command so the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And what I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and put it in her gullet and cut with it a part of the trachea of the lung, and I was called to the cure of her, and I brought back the woman as if she was dying, and uncovered the wound and brought back the blood which was emitted from the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not cut a vein nor guided it, and the wind was coming from the wound, and I cured her until she was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if not that she was hoarse in the voice, and after some days she returned to improvement of her dispositions.
And now I say that in the section of the epilepsy there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
Of the incision over the abscess which occurs in the throat outside, and is called a hernia of the throat.
This abscess called a hernia of the throat is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and it is common in women.
And it is according to two ways, whether it is natural or accidental.
And in the natural one it is not born of healing.
And the accidental one is according to two ways, one of which is similar to fatty nodes, and the other way is similar to an abscess that is made by the clogging of an artery, and in that one there is fear. And no cove that it be presumed to him as iron except in that which is small. And then you probe that and investigate it with the finger, and if you find that it is similar to a fatty node, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you incise it as you would with the nodes, and extract it with the thing that contains it from the skin and the bursa; and if not, then you scrutinize its whole being, and then cure the place with whatever is necessary for healing before it is healed.
Chapter XLV.
Of the incision of the kinds of nodes.
Of the nodes there are many kinds and I have already said all the kinds of them in the division.
And I will recount thus the difference between a node and an excrescence as you make a doubt.
Therefore I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and violent pains until the boiling of the superfluity is calmed; and it is complicated with putrefaction that at that hour the fever, the pain, and the heat cease.
But in a node there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that which is in its own sac, like a lion's cub.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a cheese and is made like that, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two kinds, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to as I said in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, that you examine it and investigate it at the beginning with the instrument that is called an intromes, according to as it will come its form in the chapter which is near this.
And the manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the most humid place which you find in the abscess, and you will revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the core.
And then finally your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and you extract the intromes and consider what is found in the residue of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision according to as I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the residue of the intromes there is no humidity, then you know that it is fatty.
And dry it over it with a section having the shape of a cross according to this form: as you are taught, and suspend it with pins, and exfoliate the core from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be done, and then you extract it in pieces until there remains no cause from it.
Because if from it remains no cause, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains any small part, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders and tighten the wound, and place upon it that which is cauterized, and cure it with the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you stitch the two lips of it and cure it with what encloses.
But if a pulsating vein is in it, whether it is pulsating or not, then you cauterize and moisten the place with a mixture of vitriol and lye, and let it stay straight for two or three days until you can scar the wound and that the boiling of the blood is calmed; and then return to incise that which is broken from the node.

Chapter .xlvii.
Of the cure of the nipples of men which are assembled from women.
Sometimes the nipples of some men become inflamed as they begin to be hairy, and then the nipples become inflamed, and the nipples are assembled from women, and they are far away from the pus.
And to that one who has this, it is necessary that he incisions those with a lunar section according to this form, from the line of B. to the line of G., and then he excoriates the whole thickness, and then he fills the wound with a medication of flesh color, and then he adjusts the two lips of the wound with stitching, and care for that until it is healed.
But if the nipple declines to the sides and is softened by its magnitude as it should be in women, then it is cut in two halves, its pus overflows, with two sections similar to a lunar figure, of which each one is contained in the other, as long as the major line contains the minor according to this form of the line of B. and the line of G. And then he excoriates the groove which is between the two lips of the wound, and removes the fat, and administers what we have said of the stitching and of the powders, what is necessary in the cure until it is healed.
And if you do not comply with the incision of that which it is necessary to cut due to the restlessness of the patient, and the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with a cotto submerged in corrosive ointment and leave it until that corrosive corrodes what is left of the gray matter, and then care for it until it is healed.
Chapter .xlviii.
Of the perforation of abscesses that come from the nipple.
These abscesses that come from the nipple are of the kind of scrophulas, hard, the ones that contain a skin that is sac.

Chapter .xlix.
Of the section of abscesses that occur due to artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the groove which is above it is consolidated, then many times an abscess occurs. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are due to the artery or vein: that when an abscess is due to the artery, it is long aggregated in the front of the body; and that when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it a kind of stridor.
And that one which is due to a vein is rounded and manifests on the surface of the body.
And the section over this abscess is an error, and most of all in that which is below the armpits, and in the angles, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very large, therefore, that its cure with iron should be avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or on the head, should be avoided.
But over that which is of those due to inflammation of the orifice of the artery, dissect in the groove a long section; and then pull the section with forceps and the artery, and delirate from the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then put over it a needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which causes you to be able to extract two arteries which are in the temples.
And then pierce the place which is between the two ligaments with a spatula until all the blood that is in it comes out, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer care in which it is generated power until the ligaments fall; and then care for it with suitable ointments to that until it is healed.
And if the abscess is due to a section of a vein, then you must have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the groove, and then introduce the needle below the place which you have had below your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract that from the other side, and then ligate the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of the grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle below all the abscess, following the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then cut the abscess in the middle of it until when it is issued what is in it, then you dissect the superfluity of the groove, and leave what of it is tied.
And then place on it the powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with warm compresses and poultices while it is healing.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which occurs due to a twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in the nerves when they are struck or occur due to excessive work, and in similar ways.
And it is made most in the places of the  joints or the ankle, or in any place where the joints are damaged.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is similar in color to the rest of the body, and in the majority of its positions it is  inflamed, and when it is tightly pressed with force, the patient feels like a stupor.
And it is not an abscess that is attached in the front of the body, and for this reason the chain is left, and it is damaged in every part and does not go to the parts in front or behind.
Therefore those that are in the joints should not be enclosed with iron, because it will very much worsen the contraction.
But that which is in the head or on the forehead,  it should be enclosed with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then you take it with the forceps and excise it to the root.
And if it is large, then you suspend it with a hook, and you excoriate it, and then you close it; and adjust the wound with sutures, and care for it until it is healed.
Chapter II.
Of the incision of an abscess which occurs from a boil that occurs to the belly.
And it happens to some men, boils that occur in the bellies of those and in other parts of the body of those, some of which are called funguses because of their similarity to fungi, of which the root is fine and the head of it is thick; and already the lips of those are converted, and it is of those that are small, and it is of those that are very magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts which were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white ones, of fine root.
And already the lips of those were reversed and were splitting, and humidity flowed from it all the time.
Therefore I incised those and attributed one in weight of eighteen ounces. and the other of six ounces.

Chapter III.

Chapter .lxix.
On the extraction of stones from women.
Stones in women are rarely produced.
But if a stone is found in any of them, then its cure is difficult, and it is prohibited by many methods.
One of them is that the woman must be very strong and a virgin.
And the second is that you do not find a woman well-versed who describes if she puts herself to the doctor when she is chaste, or is of the women having husbands.
The third is that you do not find a woman well-versed in this art, especially the operation with a hand.
And the fourth is that the place of the incision over the stone in women is far from the place of the stone, because it is feared that the incision is premature, and in that there is fear.
But if necessity compels you to do so, then you must take a female doctor well-versed, and few are found.
But if you are deprived of that, then seek a male doctor skilled and subtle, or present a woman matron well-versed in the ways of women, or a woman who in this art has been divided by the art.
Therefore, do that presentation, and command him to do all that you tell him, from the inquiry about the stone to the beginning; the reason for this is that he should regard if the woman is a virgin, then he must put his finger in her anus and want the stone.
Therefore, if that is found, force that from her, and then command him to insert over that.
But if she is not a virgin, then command the matron to insert her finger into the vagina of the patient and inquire about the stone, because she places her left hand on the bladder, and comprehend that with good comprehension.
Therefore, if that is found, then command her to gradually withdraw that from the orifice of the bladder to the parts below with the sum of her virtue until it reaches the root of the vagina.

And know that the species of stones are many: for some are small and large, and sharp and rough, and long and round, and having ramps.
Therefore, you know how many species are of it by what you signify about what you want.
And if you see a flow of blood, adjust in the place vitriol trissated and take that for an hour until the blood is abstained, and then return to your operation until the stone is ejected.

And count those, whether they are multiplied, one second, and they are separated by the sac, distinguish those among the ligaments in the umbilical cord of each of them, and sometimes they are laid as if it were one fetus with a slight natural movement, and they are born sometimes with a movement not laudable as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult during childbirth and come to what we have said of unnatural figures, then take care of them as we have recounted.
And if the midwife is skillful and makes what is done with facility and subtlety, and with tardiness, and is ingenious according to all figure according to what is prepared for her by the mind leading to health.
Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and is aborted.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and even ten, and I have already verified that one woman aborted six, and another gave birth to ten, the cause of which was made by the measurement of the glorious wise men.
And all this covers that which is in the science of the midwife, for it is very important to that appearance of this, and therefore one pauses to it as much as one should.

Of the extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the medicine and it is not outside, and you are forced to use the operation with your hand, then consider if the woman is of sound virtue and is not with any of the accidents for which she is feared to be harmed.
Then, the woman must be laid upon her back on her two, and her head be inclined downwards and her thighs be elevated.
And the minister should have those two parts or be tied on the bed so that the body of him does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother with humid oils and with a mucilage of althea and fennel and the seeds of the lily.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and then introduces her hand with facility into the mother, and then seeks with the hand the place in which the forceps are placed in the fetus.
And convenient places in this: therefore you consider if the fetus is prepared that descends upon its head, and then you place the forceps in its heels, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or even the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the proper places of the back, or even the hypochondria.
But if the descent is upon the feet of it, then in the pelvis, or in the middle of the back.
And it is necessary that you have the forceps with the right hand, and place the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and introduce the hand with facility and place the forceps in one of those places which we have said, until you reach the left cause.
And then pause and place in the opposite position of it another forceps, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction be equal, and not be an extension according to its rectitude alone.
And be careful to all parts, so that the movement of it be alleviated as it is done in every part of the eradication of it.
And it is necessary in it that which is between them the extension be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces those expertly and revolves with those which are retained.
Therefore, if the part of the fetus is laid, then the forceps are changed into the place which is higher; and do so until the whole fetus is laid.
But if the hand is inside the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then it is necessary to wrap a cloth over it; and then extract it until the whole is laid, and incise it either at the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And so you must do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is an accident to it in the movement, or there is water adjusted in the head of it, then it is necessary to introduce between the fingers the spatula and split the head and extract the water, or that which disgorges it with an instrument which is called “alundat”, the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next to this.
And similarly, if the bone is of great size by nature: and then when the bone is inserted into the wound, or that bone is placed as we have said; and then extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head is pulled out and is constricted by the collarbone, then it is split so that the moisture which is in the feet is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obstructed by such things, then you cut the head as soon as it is possible to you.
And if the bowels of the belly are festering or are in it hydropic, then you must pierce that so that the moisture which is in it runs out.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the traction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the womb is lighter.
But if it is constricted by the belly and the feet, then you must extract that with a cloth which you will have wrapped over your hand, and that you make the belly and the feet so that water runs out of those.
But if the other members are seized and the head returns, then the midwife inserts her left hand; but if the mouth of the womb is closed, then she inserts her hand into the perineum, and seeks with that the head, and pulls that with her fingers into the mouth of the womb, and then inserts into it a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mouth of the womb is constricted by an abscess caused by the heat, then it is not to be rubbed on it; but it is to be administered with an infusion of moist fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fetus is on its side, then if possible, it is to be pricked: and it is to be administered with the water that we have said in the living fetus.
And if that is not possible, then it is to be incised in pieces, and it is to be extracted.
And you must not leave any cause of the second birth.
And when you have completed your entire operation, then administer the water that we have said for the cure of the abscesses caused by the heat of the womb.
And if there occurs a flow of blood, then send them down in styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in the womb of whom was a dead fetus, and then on that same fire another pregnancy, and then the dead fetus is another. It happened to me a long time ago an abscess in his navel; and it inflated so that it opened, and began to throw out pus.
And I was called to the cure of him, and medicated him for a long time, and the plague was not consolidated.
Then I placed on him some causes of plasters of strong attraction, and extracted a bone from him, and after passing some days, I extracted another bone; and I was too amazed, as in the belly there were no bones.
And then I thought that they were from the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore, I continued to treat the abscess, and extracted from it many bones, the woman existing in her usual dispositions, and already living in that manner for a long time, correcting her a little bit of pus.
And I do not affirm that this is strange, but that in this there is science and help to that which the physician artifices with his hand for the cure administers.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of a verge with which the womb is opened:
This is the form of a stretcher in which the boards are fitted, at the fitting of which there are two verges in two extremities of two feet. But however, this verge must be more subtle of a stricture, and be made either of ebony or of a beam of wood.
And its width of each beam is two fingers and the margin of each is one finger, and the length of each is one palm and a half; and in the middle place of the two beams there are two adjustments of that same beam, the length of which is the majority of one palm and a little more, and the width of each is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the womb so that it may be opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed verges.
Another form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or wood beams according to the resemblance of forceps. But however, at the extremity of it there are two additions as you see, and the length of those additions is about one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the womb with those, then you make the woman lie on her back with her feet dangling, open that which is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, evenly according to the quantity that you want of the opening of the mouth of the womb until the midwife makes it so that you want.
